    <li> Got this kit for about $8.50 at a Wal-Mart.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And, considering the price, its an awesome value.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here&#x27;s the thing about brush shaving, its really nice.  It feels good on your face, it results in a nice close shave, and its honestly kinda fun to do it the old school way.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The bad part is, you go on the internet and find out that there&#x27;s a super elite group of people who will tell you that THIS brand of shave soap is the best soap and you should only use THIS brand of badger brush because the other types don&#x27;t compare and how you can only use THIS kind of razor because the other kinds will somehow destroy your face and make shaving the kind of unspeakable horror only sick, twisted people dare entertain their minds with.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The point I&#x27;m trying to make is this:  there is actually a community of shaving snobs.  People who&#x27;ve actually invested over a hundred dollars in particular, elite equipment to SCRAPE LITTLE HAIRS OFF THEIR CHINS!!!!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So they see this cheapo set and turn their noses up at it, because its ONLY EIGHT DOLLARS and you can BUY IT AT WAL-MART!!!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I do like wet shaving.  Its a good shave.  I shave with a double edge safety razor (a Merkur) and this particular kit.  And it works out GREAT!!!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So here&#x27;s my review:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE BRUSH:  Its a boars hair brush, and its fine.  It lathers well, it works the way it should, its not rough on my face at all.  Yes, it has a plastic handle.  WHO CARES?!?!?!?!  Its the HANDLE of a friggin BRUSH!!!  Do your hands start on fire if they touch plastic?  Do you get an allergic reaction if your fingertips handle a brush thats not metal or wood?  If you answered \\&quot;No\\&quot; to both those questions, then you&#x27;re fine.  Complaining about the material of a shaving brush handle makes you a snob.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE BOWL:  Its a bowl.  The soap sits in it, it holds steady when you lather.  Its fine.  You know why? Because its a FREAKIN&#x27; BOWL!!!  How do you honestly complain about a bowl?  It functions, it doesn&#x27;t offend the eye, its fine.  Don&#x27;t be a snob.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THE SOAP:  Honestly, I&#x27;ve tried so many canned shaving creams its ridiculous.  I&#x27;m a man with sensitive skin and it doesn&#x27;t matter how moisturizing the cream was, I still had nicks and cuts and irritated skin.  So imagine my surprise to find this soap to be a key part of a very clean, enjoyable shave.  I seriously get better results from this soap than I do with my gels and creams.  Way to go, VDH shaving soap.  Are there better shaving soaps?  Probably.  Do I care?  No, because this one leaves my face moisturized and refreshed, costs 1.80 per bar, and I can actually get it without ordering it over the internet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;BOTTOM LINE:  A great wet shave kit, especially for the price.  Avoid the snobby opinions and give it an honest shot.  If you&#x27;re not a total tool you&#x27;ll probably be surprised by how nice this kit is.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are plenty of things in this world where the level of craftsmanship and attention to detail make a huge difference.  Guitars are such a product.  Automobiles are another.  Shaving brushes and bowls are NOT!!!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Don&#x27;t be a dumb shaving snob, just go shave your face, then start investing yourself in something thats actually important.on&#x27;t be a snob.    THE SOAP:  Honestly, I&#x27;ve tried so many canned shaving creams its ridiculous.  I&#x27;m a man with sensitive skin and it doesn&#x27;t matter how moisturizing the cream was, I still had nicks and cuts and irritated skin.  So imagine my surprise to find this soap to be a key part of a very clean, enjoyable shave.  I seriously get better results from this soap than I do with my gels and creams.  Way to go, VDH shaving soap.  Are there better shaving soaps?  Probably.  Do I care?  No, because this one leaves my face moisturized and refreshed, costs 1.80 per bar, and I can actually get it without ordering it over the internet.        BOTTOM LINE:  A great wet shave kit, especially for the price.  Avoid the snobby opinions and give it an honest shot.  If you&#x27;re not a total tool you&#x27;ll probably be surprised by how nice this kit is.    There are plenty of things in this world where the level of craftsmanship and attention to detail make a huge difference.  Guitars are such a product.  Automobiles are another.  Shaving brushes and bowls are NOT!!!      Don&#x27;t be a dumb shaving snob, just go shave your face, then start investing yourself in something thats actually important.</li>

    <li> TLDR: Just starting out? Buy this set now. /TLDR    I picked this set up at the Wally a few years ago when I first started wet shaving. It&#x27;s a superb value. I keep saying I&#x27;m going to get myself a more expensive synthetic brush, but time and again I can never really justify it with this one working so well.    I didn&#x27;t care for the bowl. My first shave bowl had little ribs on the inside to keep your soap from spinning around uselessly as you try to whip up lather. This one does not. I also found it to be a little small for building up a really nice lather. But at the time I was not aware that you could melt the soap into the bottom of the bowl, which conveniently solves both problems. Your soap will stay put and it will make the bowl seem bigger since there won&#x27;t be a bunch of wasted space under your soap puck.    If you are considering getting started with wet shaving just buy it. But it now. It&#x27;s less than ten bucks! You can always upgrade later, but why agonize for hours (or days) over what brand of brush and soap to buy when you have a perfectly good set that you could run out to the store and pick up today.</li>

Yeah everyone has a \\&quot;favorite\\&quot; brand, but this is noones least favorite that I know of.  Or buy a variety pack and try out different ones till you like one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So in General, an expensive set should cost you:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Mug: N/A use anything&lt;br /&gt;Soap: $5&lt;br /&gt;Brush: $70&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So about $90 with shipping.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If it&#x27;s something you&#x27;ll use for years to come (after trying out this pack to see if you will), even it it&#x27;s a tiny fraction better, why not?  Why are some people here acting like $100 means life or death?...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Where you&#x27;ll save in wet shaving is the blades.  The general consensus for a good shave is each blade lasts you 3 shaves, or 3 days.  A pack of 100 is about $22 dollars, about.  So that&#x27;s 300 days, or close to 10 months for $22 dollars.  $22 dollars wont even buy you a Gillette fusion refill these days where I live... And let&#x27;s be honest, we usually take such bad care of it that those blades last like a week or two.  At least with this you can just throw away the blade.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Someone said \\&quot;blah blah to use to scrape hair off your chin\\&quot;...  If only it was that simple, as most of us men know, shaving is an every day thing, a part of our lives.  If you&#x27;re going to do something EVERY... SINGLE... DAY... and you&#x27;ve used this box to see if you like this method, why not spend $60 dollars for a brush even if it is a tiny little bit better, and $5 for a soap that will last you 5months to a year... The $5 dollars is worth just the fun of trying out a new thing...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Just DON&#x27;T expect this magical thing with the expensive versions, and if you&#x27;re on a tight budget, this will hold you through for a while!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EXTRA:  If you find a way to hold the brush upside down (the proper way), the water will seep down and extend the life and use of the brush. I&#x27;ve recently switched to the Omega Stipely Badger brush and I&#x27;ll give you a true non-snob comparison.     The Omega is softer and feels soft like something a woman could use to apply blush with while this boar brush feels more firm like an outdoor paint brush, a little firm but still smooth at the tips (you can wash your car with it and it wouldn&#x27;t scratch the paint). Some say badger brushes smell like...well, dead badger. Mine didn&#x27;t but it did lose a lot of the die they used to make the hair black. This lasted for 2 shaves and stopped completely. To be clear it wasn&#x27;t like emptying a pen in the sink it was more like a light graying of the typically white lather when I rinsed out the brush. Oh, and the brush is still black.    The big difference between the brushes is how they lather and how they wear. The Omega makes a smooth thick warm lather than holds well on your face and lasts the whole shave. With the same effort the boar brush produces a thinner more watery lather. I can work at it longer but it just doesn&#x27;t get there  and/or stay warm. If I never bought the badger brush I doubt this would have really mattered but it is a noticeable difference. All in all I give the boar 3 stars and the Omega 4 as I wish it was a little more firm. As for wear, the badger brush dries like a used paint brush curled at the ends and stuck together, it never goes back to the straight hair look of day 1, where as the badger returns to looking new, daily. (I always rinse my brushes thoroughly and hang them bristles down to dry.( So if the badger lasts 3 times as long the price difference is negligible.) I wont spend more than $30 on a brush so this is where my journey ends. I&#x27;m very happy with all the products mentioned but still use cheap gillette custom plus 3 disposables when I&#x27;m in a hurry.     <li> First, brush shaving may not be for everyone, I can&#x27;t see how though.    If you want to introduce a friend to brush shaving, this is the way to go.  If they don&#x27;t like it, no loss, if they do, this will carry them through until they get a better set.    As far as brushes go, if you&#x27;re buying boar, you aren&#x27;t going to waste your money on a metal or wooden handle brush!  You&#x27;re going inexpensive (not cheap).    The soap in this kit is actually quite nice.  I&#x27;m currently using a EJ Sea-Buckthorn soap, but the VDH soap must&#x27;ve been loaded with aloe, because it always makes my skin smooth, it doesn&#x27;t have a strong scent though.    The bowl in this kit (not a mug ~ a bowl) is very deep, which I actually really like.  I place my brush in the bowl and fill it to the brim with STEAMY HOT water and let it soak for 15 or 30 seconds.  It softens the soap for getting on the brush quickly and gets the brush nice and warm to the core.    At this price, pick up a few and pass them around to guys who are still in the dark about brush shaving, you&#x27;ll make some converts.    I like to leave my Edwin Jagger set at home, I have this VDH set packed in my travel kit.    For the money, it should have more stars, but compared to other shave brushes, it could have less.  Factor the cost and the product and it gets 3 stars.  Don&#x27;t mind spending $25 or more?  Go with badger.</li>

    <li> The reviews that I read of this set was that it was a good beginners (which I am) who needed an easy intro to wet shaving. While this may be true, there are some things other beginners should know before purchasing:     1. The Brush: I expected it to be less than stellar, but I feel like I&#x27;m scrubbing my face with a wet broom, or a big tooth brush. It&#x27;s bristles also started coming off right as I opened the packaging. However, it worked really well for the technique I used for lathering (see below).    2. The Soap: I initially had trouble getting a good lather from this bowl because I was trying to get the tips of the brush soapy, and then lather into a hot bowl. However, I got much better results by soaking the puck in a coffee mug with the brush for in hot water for a few minutes, pouring out the water, and then lathering directly on the soap in the mug (for a demonstration of this, check out sombercoyote&#x27;s video on Williams Soap lathering on YouTube--it&#x27;s exactly what I did). With this technique, the boar hair bristles are pretty effective so I may not pitch it quite yet.    3. The Bowl: The bowl is actually pretty nice, though it may be too shallow for the lathering method I used. It may work for others, but I think my bowl will just be used to hold my razor and brush for now.    In short, if you&#x27;re looking to start DE or straight razor shaving, this is an okay set. However, there is the [[ASIN:B004VW59DG Van Der Hagen Men&#x27;s Luxury, Shave Set, **BONUS**, set includes TWO full size 3.5oz scented soaps]] which seems more legit. It&#x27;s gotten better (albeit fewer) reviews than this one. It also comes with a stand that holds your razor and brush, which is neat. It also has a mug that seems a little deeper than this bowl, which would be ideal for me. But it&#x27;s also almost quadruple the price. The set I&#x27;m reviewing is good for practice, but I&#x27;ll be upgrading as soon as I can&#x27;t stand it any longer (starting with the brush!).    One last note: now that I&#x27;ve started to figure this set out, I wish I had simply found the components separately. Instead of buying another kit, I may just buy better components separately one at a time, especially since the mug that I&#x27;m using was essentially free. This would be much easier than dealing with the disappointment of a cheap kit like this one ;-)    Good luck!</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been a user of the VDH Shave Set for years (yes...the same brush and bowl). I also use shave creams as well([[ASIN:B0006O2K1C Geo F. Trumper Violet Soft Shaving Cream 200g cream]])([[ASIN:B002QFZ1QK Taylor of Old Bond Street Avocado Shaving Cream]])([[ASIN:B0031OXOBE Taylor of Old Bond Street Almond Shaving Cream]]) but shave soaps are so much easier to take on vacation or to the gym.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is the GED graduate of shaves sets (General Education Diploma aka the \\&quot;Good Enough Diploma\\&quot;). It&#x27;s not that $300 chromed shave set, but in the neighborhood of $10.00 it&#x27;s definitely good enough. In the right hands this kit will give you a great shave. Are there better sets on the market? Probably. Are they going to improve YOUR shaving experience to the nTH degree...probably not. Are they marketed at this price. No. Save your money and spend it on a decent razor and blades. Once you have that down...then you can experiment with pricier sets if YOU want.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I own several brushes that I&#x27;ve collected over the years because I&#x27;m just that kind of a person. The VDH set is my work horse and I now rotate brushes for the sake of rotating brushes. Some brushes are softer...others more coarse. Some brushes are not PETA friendly, some are.  In the end, the brushes I own all give me a great lather and serve their purpose. The VDH brush is no exception. Decent brush, great price and it comes with a bowl and a soap cake.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I used to break out horribly after shaving using the mass marketed stuff with rash and irritation. I then discovered wet shaving with a dual edge safety blade([[ASIN:B002CLDUZM Merkur Heavy Duty Razor with Slant Bar #198 3\\&quot;]]) and WOW what a difference. If you are able to use the Mach-50 or whatever they call them these days more power to you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Back when I first started shaving I&#x27;d use the same razor cartridge for the entire school year...rust deposits and all. I also used to feel light headed after half of a bottle of beer. Sadly those days are gone and my beard would now give a cheese grater a run for its money.  Canned shaving cream also seemed to fall short and made the whole shaving experience a royal pain in the patella as it became more drying and irritating to my skin as my beard matured. Again . . . if you can get away with the canned stuff count yourself very fortunate. In my late teens a can of shaving cream would last me a whole year. Go figure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To each his own as far as his methods are concerned. I will share mine, but I think everone&#x27;s skin/hair is different. Here&#x27;s what I think of this kit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Brush:&lt;br /&gt;My VDH brushes look nothing like the exploded cigar sunflower thing in one of the pictures above. Hmmm...(stroking imaginary chin hair...you know...because this is a review about a shave set). I can&#x27;t speak for VDH&#x27;s quality control BUT I do own 2 separate sets purchased from 2 different stores in 2 different counties.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve gifted a few of these to young men in my family new to shaving and it gives me great pleasure to see these kits on their sinks when I stop by for a visit. Maybe I&#x27;m just really lucky...even though I play the lottery weekly and never win anything.  I would think that if a brush fell apart within a few weeks that I would be able to return/exchange the product quite easily due to a manufacturer defect, but some people aren&#x27;t into returning things.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you&#x27;re new to wet shaving and don&#x27;t know how to use and care for a shave brush then google is a great resource. Basically don&#x27;t be a mongoloid and it should give you many years of great use (barring any manufacturer defects that I have yet to experience on my end).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;How do you use it? Wash your face first! Do you really want to scrape a piece of metal across a dirty, oily layer of skin? The handle of the brush fits in your palm and your fingers should grip the sides of the bristles near the base of the handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You don&#x27;t need to crush the bristles in an attempt to create a lather. After you&#x27;re done shaving gently wipe the sides of the brush on a towel to remove any water from the surface. Place the brush on a shaving brush stand ([[ASIN:B0006O4NRQ Muehle Tortoise Shaving Brush Holder]]) and allow it to dry properly in an open location (not in the medicine cabinet). The stand does not need to be super expensive. I own one similar to the link I provided that I found on ebay for a few dollars shipped. You do need a stand. Placing the brush on its handle will definitely ruin the bristles in a hurry as the moisture won&#x27;t have anywhere to go but into the handle.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve experienced the loss of a stray bristle here and there and chalked it up to wear and tear. Do I scream \\&quot;shenanigans!\\&quot; when I need new tires on my car after 60,000 miles despite good upkeep, frequent alignments, and regular tire rotating and balancing? Negative. At this price I don&#x27;t see why anyone would complain about replacing a brush after a few years of use.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I usually wet the brush and use it to moisten my face. I then wet the brush again and work up a lather on the brush using the soap in the bowl. This action allows for exfoliation and helps lifts the hair away from your face prior to shaving.  I then apply the lather for a minimum of 2 shaving passes. More often 3. When I have a date night planned I go the extra mile with a 4th pass. Yes. This means shaving multiple times in different directions. More passes paired with poor technique will leave you with nicks, cuts, and possible razor burn/rash. Use caution. If you do cut yourself it is wise to invest in a Styptic Pencil([[ASIN:B000YM76VU Pinaud Clubman styptic pencil for nick relief - 0.25 oz, 2 pack]]). They can be found for under $2.00 at your local W-Mart. They stop bleeding fast, disinfect and don&#x27;t take up much room. They work wonders! They&#x27;re advertised as sting-free. But this should be read as \\&quot;stings for free.\\&quot;  Nevertheless...the thing works!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I shave in a certain order. Top to bottom. Back to front. Front to back. Bottom to top. Shaving against the grain is the most irritating step if you&#x27;re not careful or if your skin just isn&#x27;t ready for it. If your skin is already irritated don&#x27;t irritate it further by shaving against the grain right away. Wait until the irritiation goes down.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Follow up with a toner based bump preventer ([[ASIN:B000S92OCK B&amp;C Skin Tight Product for Razor Bumps &amp; Ingrown Hairs-Extra Strength(12 oz)]] - can be found at W-Mart for fairly decent price) on a cotton pad if you&#x27;re prone to razor bumps and then after shave if you&#x27;d like ([[ASIN:B002PIPIHK Shea Moisture, Tea Tree Herbal Bump Preventer After Shave Elixir 4 oz Nubian Heritage]]). Lastly apply a shaving lotion ([[ASIN:B007OCA3UE Shea Moisture Shave Anti-aging Moistuizer &amp; Bump Preventer 2fl Oz]]). If you stick with a routine your skin will be clear, your face soft, and your woman happy.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Another option to after shave is to use an alum block after you&#x27;re done shaving (I used one when I first started wet shaving and go back to it from time to time if I experience any skin irritation or acne). Simply rinse your face with cool water. Wet the alum block with cool water. Rub the alum block on your face. Air dry. This does a few things. Disinfects, stops any bleeding, and dries to form a protective layer on your face for those of us prone to break outs or irritation post shave. Air drying keeps any lint, dust, or bacteria present on our less than fresh face towel off of ourface. If your too heavy on an application, just rub it off with clean hands and apply a thinner coat next time around. The alum block&#x27;s mild sting doubles as a critique of any flaws in your shaving technique or a dull blade that needs to be changed. Here is a link to the product available on Amazon: [[ASIN:B004QVCIKE Alum Block by Osma - 2 Pack Value]].&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Bowl:&lt;br /&gt;Ummm. Yeh. CHECK!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In all seriousness the bowl fits pretty nice in the palm of your hand while you&#x27;re lathering up. It&#x27;s easy to clean. It&#x27;s round. I&#x27;ve never eaten from it. Great job on the bowl VDH!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Soap:&lt;br /&gt;The soap is of pretty decent quality and if it causes you irritation then it&#x27;s simply not for you. I have very sensitive skin and this shave soap has never really caused me any grief. There is a learning curve to wet shaving so be careful not to blame a poor technique and routine on a good product. VDH soap has a pleasant fragrance to it and it leaves my skin feeling refreshed. It is my opinion that its fragrance is mild enough that it will not clash with an after shave.  I usually use an aftershave, and it&#x27;s the only thing I can smell after application.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Using quality products like this make shaving a little more enjoyable. If I had another face I&#x27;d be in for 2 more sets!!!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I shave with the Merkur Slant Razor that uses safety dual edge blades, for those that are curious. The other products I&#x27;ve listed in my review have all worked well for my skin although I have used others depending on sales and availability of products.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5 stars for this kit, its price range and for its quality.</li>
    <li> I bought this set a while ago at my local supermarket for about $11, and now I see it at other chains and Walmart for about $9.&lt;br /&gt;The best part about this is the soap which you can get for $2 or less retail.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The soap is good. I have yet to try other soaps/creams but it is leaps and bounds better than all the Gillette gels I used to use  like Mach, Fusion, etc. To get the benefit you need to spend at least a full minute working the lather compared to the 5 seconds it takes to put a canned gel. Don&#x27;t use too much water, just soak the brush, shake off the excess water, work the tips gently against the soap and when it starts to lather, move the action to your face. It is time well spent. My face feels better and the final judge, my wife, commented that my skin looks better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The brush is poorly made.     <li> I started with this exact set about a year ago. The box is small so look carefully&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I still use the bowl, I let it sit in hot water with the brush in it as well, I prep my face and then empty the water out but do not shake out the brush. Take the brush, put the soap just on the tips and run it around inside the bowl for about 1 minute and you will get lather like you have never seen or felt before. You can also put the soap in an old coffee mug then get the brush tips soaped and move to the bowl to create the lather or just create the lather in the cup. Either way works but doing it in the bowl keeps the soap clean that is in the mug and you can get way more lather with very little soap, in other words, you do not need much soap to get the rich lather going and since you had the bowl in the hot water, the lather will be nice and warm&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Consider most brushes like this.&lt;br /&gt;Boars Hair &#x3D; good starter brush,&lt;br /&gt;Pure Badger Hair, middle of the road brush, but definitely better than Boars Hair by a mile&lt;br /&gt;Silvertip Badger brush, definitely the top end and can be very expensive but it does make a difference&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, don&#x27;t just paint on the lather on your face, do it in circular motions for about 1 minute or two until you cannot see any skin, then to get an even coat, paint the lather on lightly, this lifts the whiskers, softens them and gets them ready for the razor. When actually shaving, do not press the razor into your skin, especially a DE razor, just let the weight of the razor glide over your skin and use short strokes, like and inch or a tad more. I typically do two passes, one north/south, the second south/north and I do not get any razor burn or bumps. On date night, I&#x27;ll do a third pass,which is across the grain. My GF loves when I do the third pass, I end up with a very smooth face and my 5 o&#x27;clock shadow comes around the next morning&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Finally, all brushes should be hung with the hair pointing down, if you put them on their handle which points the hairs up, the hairs will spread out, the water will soak into the handle and you could and will prematurely wear out the brush and possibly end up with mold or mildew in the hairs, especially if you do not shave every day. You can also clean the brush with a good shampoo, remember, it is actual hair, not fake so it can be cleaned and conditioned just like your own haird warm&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Consider most brushes like this.&lt;br /&gt;Boars Hair &#x3D; good starter brush,&lt;br /&gt;Pure Badger Hair, middle of the road brush, but definitely better than Boars Hair by a mile&lt;br /&gt;Silvertip Badger brush, definitely the top end and can be very expensive but it does make a difference&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Also, don&#x27;t just paint on the lather on your face, do it in circular motions for about 1 minute or two until you cannot see any skin, then to get an even coat, paint the lather on lightly, this lifts the whiskers, softens them and gets them ready for the razor. When actually shaving, do not press the razor into your skin, especially a DE razor, just let the weight of the razor glide over your skin and use short strokes, like and inch or a tad more. I typically do two passes, one north/south, the second south/north and I do not get any razor burn or bumps. On date night, I&#x27;ll do a third pass,which is across the grain.     <li> To begin with, I have some criticisms of this product.      First of all; the brush.  The brush is cheaply made.  Saying that, though, does not make me a snob as some other reviewers might suggest.  The truth is that it frays easily and the hairs start falling out of the handle after only a few uses.  Don&#x27;t expect the brush to last more than a month or so, even if you take care of it properly and store it upside down.  Also, this brush is made from Boar hair, rather than Badger hair.  Boar hair is more scratchy and prickly on the face, and doesn&#x27;t hold water as well as Badger hair.    Secondly, the soap.  The soap is not bad, it makes for a smooth shave and has a nice, very subtle scent to it.  The only negative I have to say about it is that it would be better if the kit came with a glycerin soap.  Van Der Hagen does make a glycerin soap, but apparently not as part of a kit.    The bowl is fine, it has a nice weight and I really have nothing bad to say about it.    Despite my criticisms this product is still great for guys who are new to the wet shaving technique and want to try it without spending too much money.  Even with the somewhat mediocre brush, this will still give you a closer and smoother shave than normal shaving cream.  If you use a safety razor as well it&#x27;s even better.  Try this kit and if you like it after a few weeks upgrade to a real badger brush, there are some available on here for less than $20.     <li> About 15 years ago, a co-worker turned me on to brush shaving, and I never turned back. I broke in with the brush and soap from Van Der Hagen (they were separate, not in a set). I no longer have to bother with canned shaving creams, and I just love the old school feel of shaving with a brush and soap. In the end, it&#x27;s less expensive, as the soap cake lasts much longer than a can of cream/gel and are individually less expensive. I&#x27;d love to start using a straight razor also, but I&#x27;m a little scared...HA HA! The brush will last if you care for it properly - after use, rinse and shake it out, and store it hanging bristles down (gravity will draw water/moisture away from the base, as otherwise it rots out the base and causes the hairs to fall out prematurely). So if you want to start brush shaving, or maybe are looking for a low-cost travel set, I&#x27;d go with this set.</li>

    <li> Quite good for a shave set and an incredible price. You don&#x27;t need a fancy soap or brush or a fancy bowl to build a great lather. For me that means I melt the soap down into the bowl and load up the brush in there before I face lather and get a good lather going. After I am done with each area shaving I re-apply lather there by painting it on as I noticed I get a better shave doing that as it keeps my beard moisturized and some of the ingredients in the soap soften the beard, so better shave. After I am done with all areas i whip up a proper lather on my face and go for my second pass and any touch ups I need to do afterwards and I am good.</li>
    <li> Yes, the brush is not good, but the bowl and soap worth it. The value exceed the price.&lt;br /&gt;Like another user wrote, put it in microwave and it will get the shape of the bowl. Just take care not to over heat it.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;m new to safety razors (been shaving with an Edwin Jagger DE89 for about two weeks) so I decided to pick this kit up to see what all the hoopla was about using a brush and puck soap. So, I had to pick out the boar hairs from my freshly lathered face before I began my shave. I did like the feeling of the bristles against my skin. I can&#x27;t say if that brush massage helped get a better shave or if it&#x27;s just a \\&quot;feel good\\&quot; routine.   The soap: Before I got this soap, I used a canned shaving gel and applied it to my face using my hand. The gel felt much better against my skin and moisturized my skin way better than the included soap. Oil of Olay bath soap does a much better job at moisturizing my skin than this puck soap. After my shave, my skin felt more irritated and my skin felt drier using this puck soap than using the canned shaving gel. With the gel, the razor seemed to glide smoothly across my face. It seemed like there was a bit more resistance against my face using the puck, which could be the cause of my irritated skin.   The bowl: It&#x27;s a bowl. Unlike a mug, it doesn&#x27;t have a handle, so it can be a little trickier to hold if you have slippery hands. I could have pulled out an unused mug and been happier and saved some money.  So in the end, I spent $10 for a brush massage and irritated skin. I&#x27;m right back where I started. I still don&#x27;t know if using a brush is for me. To find this out, I may have to bite the bullet and spend the money on a quality setup. But until then, I&#x27;m perfectly happy using my canned shaving gel.</li>

    <li> My main thoughts: This product costs what shaving products should cost. It&#x27;s nice to see this in a market that seems wildly expensive to newcomers. All elements of the kit are durably made. Good way to see if you like shaving with a brush, which you probably will.  1. About the physical product:  Brush:  - Not too rough or too soft.  - Well-glued. In my case, the brush looked nothing like that poorly glued specimen in the product photos.  - Takes a little while to dry. Make sure to dry with the bristles hanging down (see below).  Bowl:  - Solid and a lot heavier than I expected. I could probably drop this and it would be fine.  - Nice thick glossy finish.  Soap:  - Subtle, pleasant smell.  - Good for sensitive skin. Better than my Aveeno can.  - Builds lather decently, might take more time than some are used to (see below).  - Perhaps as many uses as a can of shaving cream.  2. Tips to make the product even better:  - Make your own brush stand. Take a coat hanger from the dry cleaners, fold the shoulders in, and kink the hanger loop forward. It will exponentially lengthen your usage time and will allow the brush to fully dry after use. Yes, this is a lower quality brush, so you&#x27;ll quickly destroy it if you dry it by balancing it on its handle.  - Take your time building lather. At first, you&#x27;ll be terrible at building lather in the bowl. Take your time with it and really develop it before putting it on your face. The boar&#x27;s hair will also take a few more uses to become effective.  I bought this, along with a Concord DE razor, for a cheap introduction to safety razor shaving. I&#x27;m very happy with the start of things. I recommend it, along with some care.</li>

I leave the soap in the ceramic bowl and use the brush to lather it up before applying to the face.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here&#x27;s why it&#x27;s 3 stars and not 5: The brush doesn&#x27;t last. I&#x27;ve purchased two brushes from this brand and both of them have lasted a couple of months. I don&#x27;t know if that&#x27;s normal for other brands, but I doubt it. I am investing in a better quality brush, but I still use this ceramic bowl and soap. The soap lasts a LONG time and it&#x27;s really cheap. If you&#x27;re getting into the traditional shaving method, I&#x27;d recommend this as an economical starter option.</li>
    <li> This is the first set of items I used when trying wet shaving.  I have since purchased a badger hair brush and Proraso shave cream and find both of them much better than what comes in this set.  The soap in this set may not have enough glycerin in it to do the job.  I tried a few other soaps and found them to be better but still prefer the Proraso cream.</li>
    <li> I gave this set 4 stars because it is quite nice for the money, however if you&#x27;re a little clumsy - like me - you might drop it in the sink and break it, like I did. I ordered a stainless steel bowl to replace it, I might dent that one but I won&#x27;t break it!</li>
    <li> This shaving set is obviously designed for first time wet shavers to get their feet wet (bad pun intended) at a cheap price. Being a first timer, I fell to the appeal of it as well. Now, don&#x27;t get me wrong, it&#x27;s not bad at all. It gives you a nice little bowl, a bar of soap, and a boar&#x27;s hair brush all for the cheap price of ten bucks. It&#x27;s a great idea to have all these items packaged together so first-timers don&#x27;t get overwhelmed at having to purchase everything separately. But if you just take a step back, you might see that it&#x27;s no big deal to get these three items separately, and in fact it might be in your own benefit to do so. On the other hand, you might enjoy the learning experience you get from this package. I&#x27;ll share my critiques of each item and what I learned.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) the bowl: It&#x27;s a great bowl, but I find it a little small and sometimes lather can start foaming out of it during your mixing, no biggy. The thing I like most about this bowl is that it has a nice contrasting color to shave cream. I actually found it hard to keep track of all my created lather when I tried making it in a white bowl, but I have no trouble at all with this bowl.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) the boar&#x27;s hair brush: Ohhh, you&#x27;ll hear the \\&quot;pros\\&quot; always hating on boar&#x27;s hair brushes and saying badger hair brushes are better. I actually completely agree with them; I find a badger hair brush to be much better suited to creating and applying lather. However, I still had a lot of fun comparing the two in my shaves and learning for myself the actual differences between them. It&#x27;s not like a boar&#x27;s hair brush is useless, you can definitely still make lather with it. But if you&#x27;re a no-nonsense kind of guy and don&#x27;t want to experiment, I strongly urge you to not buy this set. You will definitely replace this brush with a badger hair brush and you&#x27;ll feel like you wasted your money.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) the soap: It&#x27;s fine. You can purchase it on its own for like 2 bucks on amazon. A good idea is to remove the puck, place it in the bowl, and then microwave in spurts of ten seconds until it melts. Now let it reharden and it will be formed to the bottom of the bowl making lather creation easier (microwave melting works fine with this type of soap, but it doesnt work for certain other types so be careful). If you&#x27;re like most people, you&#x27;ll find that lather making from a soap takes more time and is harder than creating lather from a shaving cream. If you don&#x27;t want to deal with the hardships of turning soap into lather but you still want to wet-shave, you&#x27;re probably better off buying a cream. I find it a fun skill to practice and master so I&#x27;m happy with the soap.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Conclusion: For someone who literally wants to get it right the first time with cheap but quality products, I couldn&#x27;t recommend this set. You really are better off getting the cheap tweezerman $10 badger hair brush, getting a cheap bowl/mug from wherever, and just buying this soap separately. However, for someone who is interested in learning and doesn&#x27;t mind trying out a boar&#x27;s hair first, then I whole-heartedly recommend this set. I don&#x27;t see boar&#x27;s hair brushes sold individually on amazon, and they&#x27;re like 10 bucks at stores, so this set really is a great deal. In addition to it, I still recommend you buy the tweezerman badger hair brush. You&#x27;ll have a much better understanding of the comparison between a badger hair and a boar hair brush if you try both out for yourself, and at twenty bucks (10 for this set and 10 for the additional badger hair brush) it&#x27;s a great affordable way to get into the world of wet shaving.</li>
    <li> Awesome Soap and bowl, the brush is on the lower end of quality but this was my first attempt at wet shaving so this was a great deal for just trying out, the handle of the brush did not fit well in the Mission Style Wood Shave Stand for Razor and Brush - Walnut Finish but you couldnt beat the price, i have passed the brush onto my lil brother for him to try but i am still ejoying the wonderful soap and bowl... great starter but if you enjoy the wet shave you&#x27;ll soon move onto a pure badger hair brush</li>
    <li> I was frustrated with the cost of canned shaving creams and the inexpensive ones did not do a good job at all. I made an impulse purchase when I saw this at Wal-mart, although I really liked the shave I got using hair conditioner, I didn&#x27;t care for the smell and it didn&#x27;t leave my face feeling clean.    If you are not a shaving snob and just want a better shave than you get with canned shaving creams at a lot less cost then give this a try. I did and I am now hooked on soap and brush shaving.    Pro: It is inexpensive. It gives me a better shave than I have gotten with any canned cream. Saves me a heck of a lot of money on shaving cream. The bowl holds the soap so well that it doesn&#x27;t move around when building a lather. I really like the size of the bowl. It fits great in my big hands, I&#x27;m 6&#x27;5\\&quot;. Smells good and leaves my skin feeling soft yet clean. Brush bristles are firm enough to produce a good lather but not foamy like canned creams.    Con: I shave in the shower and since the bowl doesn&#x27;t have a lid, I have to keep the bowl on a shelve outside the shower but within reach while I&#x27;m in the shower.    Neither pros or cons: The handle of the brush is plastic. I don&#x27;t care that it is plastic because I care more about \\&quot;expensive to quality of shave\\&quot; ratio but if you are a shaving snob and want to waste you money on a wooden handle when a plastic one works great (even better than wood if you shower shave) then go else where. There is no brush holder but you don&#x27;t need one since it stands upright on the handle.    I start by running the brush under the shower then start to build the lather in the bowl but finish lathering on my face. I&#x27;ve watched videos on YouTube that show how to lather (like this one [...] ) but I think the guy in the video is nuts because I don&#x27;t need to push the brush that hard on my face or bowl as to dis-form the brush to get a good lather but then I prefer lather to foam so in my opinion the guy in the video over lathers and produces way too much foam. Foam does nothing to increase the quality of your shave. The oils in the soap help the blade glide over your face and the brush helps lift up the hairs. Producing a lot of foam is just a waste of time and will cause your brush to wear out quicker.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been using this set for about a week and I&#x27;m pretty happy with it. The brush seems to lose a bristle or two each shave, but I&#x27;m not that worried with it. If I keep at this, I&#x27;ll probably step up to a nice brush long before this one would deteriorate.     I don&#x27;t follow the directions on the box, but instead use some tips I read online...  I grabbed an old coffee mug and dropped the soap in there and kept the bowl just for lather building. Run HOT water into the bowl/brush to get it all warm, add enough hot water to the soap to just cover the indented area. Squeeze out the brush and begin working it into the soap and get it really loaded up- takes me 30secs or so of plunging/swirling it on the soap. Then I empty the hot water from my bowl and begin working up a lather in it, adding just a trickle of hot water to it as needed (you&#x27;ll have to experiment to see what works here). Once you get it how you want it- it takes me up to a minute to get a nice lather- apply it to your face using up/down strokes.    Anyway, the set seems like a good value for the money- don&#x27;t hesitate to try it for the price.</li>

It&#x27;s just something you have to get a feel for and no amount of reading will make it easier. You get the hang of how much water the brush needs, how much soap to build on the bristles, how much pressure to place on the brush, the angle to hold the brush, and the speed to whip. Considering the soap will last forever and it&#x27;s cheap to replace I would recommend practice building lather a few times till you get the hang of it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I let the brush soak in hot water for 5 min, shake off the excess water, dip the end in warm water, swirl on the soap, and build lather in my bowl.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Soap&lt;br /&gt;-----&lt;br /&gt;The soap that&#x27;s included works well. It&#x27;s a Boar&#x27;s hair brush instead of Badger.  Who cares??  Swirling a brush around a bar of soap to make thick bubbles is not rocket science.  I haven&#x27;t had any Boar&#x27;s hair injuries as far as I know.  Perhaps a badger hair brush would be better, but I haven&#x27;t found a reason to complain about this one yet.  The bowl is pretty useless.  The brush actually does a great job of building a lather on its own, despite being boar&#x27;s hair. It gives me a good lather and leaves my face silky smooth without making me smell like Old Spice aftershave.  It basically leaves me burn-free.  Bottom line -- This is a great shave set for people who want something different. In my opinion, the upscale &amp;#34;luxury&amp;#34; sets are highly overrated. If you&#x27;re new to wet shaving,  I would skip this and spring for a good badger brush and some good soap or cream.</li>

    <li> For those of you who have been shaving with a double edge \\&quot;safety razor\\&quot; for years and bought this because it was one hell of a deal... you should have known better. Is this a top of the line set? No, but for the cheap price it shouldn&#x27;t be. This set is great for beginners. I own this set myself and still use all but the soap everytime I shave. I still use the brush and bowl. I do not use the soap as it dries our my skin. I use Proraso Shave Cream instead (its amazing!) Someday I may upgrade to a badger brush, but this one still works good. At the end of the day with this kit I can build a lather, apply the lather, and get a close shave... what else is there?!? Here are some TIPS to prolong your kit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) Do not stand your brush on end using the handle while letting it dry! This will allow water to seep into the handle thus shortening the life span of the bristles. Invest in a holder to allow your brush to dry bristles down. This is the number one mistake made my new shavers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) If the soap does not work for you, try PRORASO Shave Cream (Menthol). It costs about $10-15 per 5.2 oz tube, but all you need is a dime sized drop in your bowl and you can lather up that face all morning long! A tube will last me all year long! It lathers up well with this brush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) When done shaving, rinse your brush, and squeeze all the extra water out from the brush! Again, dry in a stand with bristles down!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) Enjoy your shave! In my opinion there is no better way to start my day than with a goodclean close shave.</li>

When the supplied soap puck was worked down to a sliver, i replaced it with Colonal Conk Bay Rum soap and noticed a huge difference in the amount of lather the brush built up. I have also replaced my gillete fusion with a highly rated double edged safety razor, and believe that the qualiity of the shave is about the same as the fusion, but cost of razors is so cheap that the cost of the safety razor and 5 blades was less than two four cartridge replacement packs of the gillete fusion.     <li> The boar-bristle brush hard-wearing, but doesn&#x27;t really give you a good lather. I got the best results as follows: Wash your face with warm (not hot) water and leave it wet. If you have hard water, soak the brush with cold/room temperature water and set the bristles to drip into the sink. If you have soft/distilled water, you can use warm/hot water more effectively. rather than cutting pieces of the soap into the dish like most tutorials will tell you, take the brick of soap out of the plastic and put it in the mug it will stick in place after a few uses. After ~ 30 seconds, or the brush stops dripping, swirl the tips (ONLY the tips) of the bristles on the surface of the soap until they are coated with soap. Then, swirl the brush on your wet skin where it will lather, and use the brush to spread the lather.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The soap included with the kit has this weird fat smell that I never liked, but it is very moisturizing. Muhle makes a soap with a scent that I like much better.</li>

    <li> First time &amp;#34;wet&amp;#34; shaver so no basis for comparison. Bought this alternatively from piecing together mid-high end brush/soap/bowl. Pleasantly light fragrance that doesn&#x27;t linger long (which I prefer) and IMHO doesn&#x27;t smell &amp;#34;girly&amp;#34; or &amp;#34;manly&amp;#34; AT ALL, just more of a clean soapy smell. I also like the boars hair brush, but I&#x27;ve never used a badger haired brush to compare. After some trial and error with the lathering process, I&#x27;ve found a solid system for this product that works for me: Soak the brush in the bowl with hot tap water. Also add enough hot water to cover the top of the soap cake...this will allow for quicker brush loading. Do all of this before showering if possible or at least 3 minutes prior to lathering. Dump bowl water and shake out brush 1-2 times, so just a small amount of water stays in the brush. Brush load at least 30-45+ seconds and lather in the bowl 1-2 minutes, adding a few drops of water AS NEEDED. Remember, you want a THICK and SILKY lather. Too much water will make it flat and loose. Happy shaving mates :)</li>

    <li> For men sick of the chemical tang to shaving cream and the discomfort and cost of disposable blades, the Van Der Hagen shave set makes an excellent introduction to shaving the old-fashioned wet lather method our fathers and grandfathers preferred. While technological improvements sometimes save time and effort, shaving is one arena where older is better in my opinion.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The three piece set includes a handsome green-glazed bowl, a puck of shaving soap, and a boar-hair brush with a solid plastic handle. Add one razor with good cartridges and you are set to go. Even disposable razors can be used, though the effect may not be as ideal. The complete kit is its main selling point, and at this low price, it makes an outstanding gift for someone considering making the transition. It can also make a good back-up or travel set, particularly for students living in dorms or a businessman who wants to leave his more expensive alternatives at home.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I recommend replacing the shaving soap with [[ASIN:B004XC75D6 Colonel Conk Glycerin Shave Soap Bay Rum (106g)]], which boasts a much better lather, fresher fragrance, and longer lasting soap. I was not impressed by the Van der Hagen option. The puck whips up a reasonable lather and the smell isn&#x27;t bad, but bay rum wins hands down for me any day. My fiance&#x27;s skin felt much softer and the shave looked easier. But to each, their own, and a man can never have too much shaving soap as far as I&#x27;m concerned.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The boar brush is considered a step below badger hair by connoisseurs, but for a foray into wet shaving, it works perfectly well. Most important is a shaving stand to allow the brush to dry between uses after being properly rinsed and cleaned. This kit does not include a stand, but excellent chrome options are available that fit just fine. The plastic handle is durable and comfortable for use, and resists cracking, scratches, and occasional nicks. After two years of use, my brother&#x27;s brush looked pretty good.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This set couldn&#x27;t be better priced to get started and allows the timely replacement of components once personal preferences are discovered. The results of a good shave speak for themselves, and the Van der Hagen set will help you achieve that..&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This set couldn&#x27;t be better priced to get started and allows the timely replacement of components once personal preferences are discovered. I let water sit on top of the soap to soften it up a little while I am soaking the boars brush in hot water. I then dump the excess water off the top of the soap and add 5-6 drops of glycerin (which helps in moisturizing my face) and then whip up the lather with the boars brush after shaking out excess water. I do this every day. Just to change things up so they do not get boring, once a week I add a squirt of the Barbasol arctic chill after I have worked up the lather with the shaving soap so I get the cooling feeling and smell of the menthol.rt of the Barbasol arctic chill after I have worked up the lather with the shaving soap so I get the cooling feeling and smell of the menthol.</li>

Since using up the soap that came with this set, I&#x27;ve switched to a smaller ceramic cup I had lying around to hold my puck more securely. This bowl still gets used as part of my daily shaving routine, however. I fill it with hot water to soak my brush and razor while I wet my face and apply pre-shave. Then I empty the hot water, fill my brush with soap, and lather in the bowl while it is still warm. It didn&#x27;t really break in until after the soap that came with this set was long gone. After a few months of steady use it is soft, but not too soft. It holds a substantial amount of lather, and both scrubs and applies lather well. For an inexpensive brush, the knot size is quite large. It still sheds the occasional hair, but it is a cheap brush and I&#x27;m not picky. I have a few brushes in my collection now. This is probably the cheapest one, but still sees regular rotation. For best results, let it soak in warm water for little while.</li>
